B000002UWL|5.0|For many fans, the Pet Shop Boys ARE electronic music. Before bands as disparate as the Orb, Aphex Twin, Massive Attack, Portishead and Boards of Canada redefined the way electronic and techno music were made, Pet Shop Boys delivered heart and soul to what was considered \\"mechanical music\\". The singles they made in the 80s - \\"West End Girls\\", \\"Opportunities (Let's Make Lots of Money)\\", \\"Suburbia\\", \\"What Have I Done to Deserve This?\\", \\"Always in My Mind\\", \\"Domino Dancing\\" - are seminal pop singles of that period - cerebral, complex to the point of avant-garde, yet strongly melodic and emotionally heart-lifting.<br /><br />However, the 1980s were coming to an end and the 1990s were about to begin. At the time, no one was aware of it, but the musical climate was gradually changing - the rise of West Coast rap, the slow demise of 80s hard rock and glam metal, the increasing popularity of country music and, most of all, the ascendance of grunge, which would take full effect in 1991. In addition, many pop acts that sustained success in the 80s were about to be cast off and rejected - Duran Duran, George Michael, Paula Abdul, A Flock of Seagulls, INXS, even towering figures like Michael Jackson and Prince (although the latter made a comeback in early 2000s).<br /><br />Where does the PSB fit in to all of this? They neither fell out of obscurity or become giant superstars in America. They continued doing what many maverick artists like Steely Dan, Todd Rundgren and David Bowie have done - defy expectations and make the music they wanted. The outcome? \\"Behaviour\\", an intoxicating synth-pop album that forgoes much of the catchy, beat-driven music of the 80s for a more leisurely paced, seductive sound. Gone was the dance and in came introspection. As a result, a masterpiece was born.<br /><br />In these subtle but emotionally intense ten tracks, Pet Shop Boys delivered beautifully constructed pop that showed them improving their craft and embracing maturity. The album is bookend by two of the most emotionally charged tracks the PSB had done - the cascading \\"Being Boring\\" and the melancholic \\"Jealousy\\". In between are stunners such as the dark \\"This Must Be the Place I Waited Years to Leave\\", the skeptical \\"How Can You Expect to Be Taken Seriously?\\", the relaxing \\"To Face the Truth\\", the opulent \\"My October Symphony\\" and soulful \\"The End of the World\\". All these songs deal with romantic distress, disintegrating relationships and unrequited love.<br /><br />Excellent as the album tracks are, though, the best songs of \\"Behaviour\\" remain its four singles: The ironically titled opening track, \\"Being Boring\\", remains one of the best and best-loved songs of the PSB discography and for good reason: the wistful guitar riffs, moody synthesizers and simple but effective beats make for an alluring listen, heightened by Neil Tennant's dramatic lyrics about lives changing and perceptions becoming different. \\"How Can You Expect to Be Taken Seriously?\\", one of the few songs that injects humor, satirizes a pop artist's vain attempts to be taken seriously. \\"So Hard\\", the album's first single and the only one closest to the dance-oriented music of the 1980s, addresses the futility of sexual affairs; and the majestic \\"Jealousy\\" is self-explanatory - infidelity, emotional indifference, envy, all presented with gorgeous keyboards by Chris Lowe and strings and a soulful lead performance by Tennant that turns a potentially schmaltzy ballad into a moving tale of genuine heartbreak.<br /><br />Despite being over 20 years old, \\"Behaviour\\" remains as fresh and relevant as it did back in 90, no mean feat in a genre where an older generation of electronic and pop music bands (Duran Duran, Spandau Ballet, Culture Club, Eurythimics, etc.) was about to be supplanted by the more cutting-edge bands of the 1990s like Massive Attack, the Chemical Brothers, Moby and DJ Shadow. That's because Lowe and Tennant were terrific songwriters that had a strong ear for melodies, a strong sense of musical craftsmanship and an intellect in telling stories without resorting to pop cliches or dated formulas. If there's one glaring flaw, it's that the singles are so strong that listeners will avoid the album tracks. But doing that would do \\"Behaviour\\" a giant disservice - it's a wholly terrific pop album from beginning to end and rivals \\"Actually\\" and \\"Very\\" as one of PSB's (and, by extension, electronic music's) crowning achievements. Don't hesitate to buy this, even if you don't care about electronic music.<br /><br />Strongest recommendation to buy at all costs.ong sense of musical craftsmanship and an intellect in telling stories without resorting to pop cliches or dated formulas.
